13 gasped one of the young men ; and there it was , slowly but steadily mounting the ridge itself .
14 Parents and children clung together , as if by that means they could drive back the advancing flood ; and the youth who had caused all this terrible catastrophe , seized his sweetheart , and cried : ' I will climb with you to the top of that tree , and there no waters can reach us . '
15 But , as he spoke , something cold touched him , and quickly he glanced down at his feet .
16 Then with a shudder he saw that they were feet no longer , but bird 's claws .
17 He looked at the girl he was clasping , and beheld a great black bird standing at his side ; he turned to his friends , but a flock of great awkward flapping creatures stood in their place He put up his hands to cover his face , but they were no more hands , only the ends of wings ; and when he tried to speak , a noise such as he had never heard before seemed to come from his throat , which had suddenly become narrow and slender .
18 Already the water had risen to his waist , and he found himself sitting easily upon it , while its surface reflected back the image of a black swan , one of many .
19 Never again did the swans become men ; but they are still different from other swans , for in the night-time those who listen can hear them talk in a language that is certainly not swan 's language ; and there are even sounds of laughing and talking , unlike any noise made by the swans whom we know .
20 The little Bunyip was carried home by its mother , and after that the waters sank back to their own channels .
21 The side of the XXXXX where she lives is always shunned by everyone , as nobody knows when she may suddenly put out her head and draw him into her mighty jaws .	pool		ground|holes|man|midst|pool|ridge|sound|spot|surface|waters

1 ` What could it be ? '
2 they asked one of another ; ` there was not a cloud in the sky , yet the water had risen higher already than they had ever known it do before . '
3 For an instant they stood watching as if they were frozen , then they turned and ran with all their might , the man with the Bunyip running faster than all .
4 When he reached a high peak over-looking all the plain he stopped to take breath , and turned to see if he was safe yet .
5 Safe !
6 why only the tops of the trees remained above that sea of water , and these were fast disappearing .
7 They must run fast indeed if they were to escape .
8 So on they flew , scarcely feeling the ground as they went , till they flung themselves on the ground before the holes scooped out of the earth where they had all been born .
9 The old men were sitting in front , the children were playing , and the women chattering together , when the little Bunyip fell into their midst , and there was scarcely a child among them who did not know that something terrible was upon them .

16 Father Grumbler Once upon a time there lived a man who had nearly as many children as there were sparrows in the garden .
17 He had to work very hard all day to get them enough to eat , and was often tired and cross , and abused everything and everybody , so that people called him ` Father Grumbler . '
18 By-and-by he grew weary of always working , and on Sundays he lay a long while in bed , instead of going to church .
19 Then after a time he found it dull to sit so many hours by himself , thinking of nothing but how to pay the rent that was owing , and as the tavern across the road looked bright and cheerful , he walked in one day and sat down with his friends .
20 ` It was just to chase away Care , ' he said ; but when he came out , hours and hours after , Care came out with him .

1 Then with a shudder he saw that they were feet no longer , but bird 's claws .
2 He looked at the girl he was clasping , and beheld a great black bird standing at his side ; he turned to his friends , but a flock of great awkward flapping creatures stood in their place He put up his hands to cover his face , but they were no more hands , only the ends of wings ; and when he tried to speak , a noise such as he had never heard before seemed to come from his throat , which had suddenly become narrow and slender .
3 Already the water had risen to his waist , and he found himself sitting easily upon it , while its surface reflected back the image of a black swan , one of many .
4 Never again did the swans become men ; but they are still different from other swans , for in the night-time those who listen can hear them talk in a language that is certainly not swan 's language ; and there are even sounds of laughing and talking , unlike any noise made by the swans whom we know .
5 The little Bunyip was carried home by its mother , and after that the waters sank back to their own channels .
6 The side of the pool where she lives is always shunned by everyone , as nobody knows when she may suddenly put out her head and draw him into her mighty jaws .
7 But people say that underneath the black waters of the pool she has a house filled with beautiful things , such as mortals who dwell on the earth have no idea of .
8 Though how they know I can not tell you , as nobody has ever seen it .
9 -LSB- From Journal of Anthropological-Institute . -RSB-
10 Father Grumbler Once upon a time there lived a man who had nearly as many children as there were sparrows in the garden .
11 He had to work very hard all day to get them enough to eat , and was often tired and cross , and abused everything and everybody , so that people called him ` Father Grumbler . '
12 By-and-by he grew weary of always working , and on Sundays he lay a long while in bed , instead of going to church .
13 Then after a time he found it dull to sit so many hours by himself , thinking of nothing but how to pay the rent that was owing , and as the tavern across the road looked bright and cheerful , he walked in one day and sat down with his friends .
14 ` It was just to chase away Care , ' he said ; but when he came out , hours and hours after , Care came out with him .
15 Father Grumbler entered his house feeling more dismal than when he left it , for he knew that he had wasted both his time and his money . '
16 I will go and see the Holy Man in the cave near the well , ' he said to himself , ` and perhaps he can tell me why all the luck is for other people , and only misfortunes happen to me . '
17 And he set out at once for the cave .
18 It was a long way off , and the road led over mountains and through valleys ; but at last he reached the cave where the Holy Man dwelt , and knocked at the door .
19 ` Who is there ? '
20 asked a voice from within .
21 ` It is I , Holy Man , Father Grumbler , you know , who has as many XXXXX as sparrows in the garden . '	children		children|everybody|head|luck|mother|surface|swan|things|time|waist

15 said he .

17 But when you have had enough , be sure you do n't forget to cry out : `` That will do for to-day . ''
18 Oh !

20 Do you understand ? '

1 Then after a time he found it dull to sit so many hours by himself , thinking of nothing but how to pay the rent that was owing , and as the tavern across the road looked bright and cheerful , he walked in one day and sat down with his friends .
2 ` It was just to chase away Care , ' he said ; but when he came out , hours and hours after , Care came out with him .
3 Father Grumbler entered his house feeling more dismal than when he left it , for he knew that he had wasted both his time and his money . '
4 I will go and see the Holy Man in the cave near the well , ' he said to himself , ` and perhaps he can tell me why all the luck is for other people , and only misfortunes happen to me . '
5 And he set out at once for the cave .
6 It was a long way off , and the road led over mountains and through valleys ; but at last he reached the cave where the Holy Man dwelt , and knocked at the door .
7 ` Who is there ? '
8 asked a voice from within .
9 ` It is I , Holy Man , Father Grumbler , you know , who has as many children as sparrows in the garden . '
10 ` Well , and what is it that you want ? ' '
11 I want to know why other people have all the luck , and only misfortunes happen to me ! '
12 The Holy Man did not answer , but went into an inner cave , from which he came out bearing something in his hand .
13 ` Do you see this basket ? '
14 said he .
15 ` It is a magical basket , and if you are hungry you have only got to say : `` Little basket , little basket , do your duty , '' and you will eat the best dinner you ever had in your life .
16 But when you have had enough , be sure you do n't forget to cry out : `` That will do for to-day . ''
17 Oh !
18 -- and one thing more -- you need not show it to everybody and declare that I have give it to you .
19 Do you understand ? '
20 Father Grumbler was always accustomed to think of himself as so unlucky that he did not know whether the Holy Man was not playing a trick upon him ; but he took the basket without being polite enough to say either ` Thank you , ' or ` Good-morning , ' and went away .
21 However , he only waited till he was out of sight of the cave before he stooped down and whispered : ` Little XXXXX , little basket , do your duty . '	basket		basket|children|everybody|friends|garden|nothing|rent|time|to-day|trick

8 Father Grumbler felt quite frightened at the torrent , but at last he remembered what the Holy Man had told him , and cried at the top of his voice : ` Enough !
9 enough !
10 That will do for to-day ! '
11 And the lid of the basket closed with a snap .
12 Father Grumbler sighed with relief and happiness as he looked around him , and sitting down on a heap of stones , he ate till he could eat no more .
13 Trout , salmon , turbot , soles , and a hundred other fishes whose names he did not know , lay boiled , fried , and grilled within reach of his hands .
14 As the Holy Man had said , he had never eaten such a dinner ; still , when he had done , he shook his head , and grumbled ; ` Yes , there is plenty to eat , of course , but it only makes me thirsty , and there is not a drop to drink anywhere . '
15 Yet , somehow , he could never tell why , he looked up and saw the tavern in front of him , which he thought was miles , and miles , and miles away .
16 ` Bring the best wine you have got , and two glasses , good mother , ' he said as he entered , ` and if you are fond of fish there is enough here to feed the house .
17 Only there is no need to chatter about it all over the place .
18 You understand ?
19 Eh ? '
20 And without waiting for an answer he whispered to the basket : ` Little basket , little basket , do your duty . '
21 The innkeeper and his wife thought that their customer had gone suddenly mad , and watched him closely , ready to spring on him if he became violent ; but both instinctively jumped backwards , nearly into the fire , as rolls and fishes of every kind came tumbling out of the XXXXX , covering the tables and chairs and the floor , and even overflowing into the street .	basket		Enough|Trout|basket|duty|glasses|mother|reach|salmon|sight|sort

9 The innkeeper and his wife thought that their customer had gone suddenly mad , and watched him closely , ready to spring on him if he became violent ; but both instinctively jumped backwards , nearly into the fire , as rolls and fishes of every kind came tumbling out of the basket , covering the tables and chairs and the floor , and even overflowing into the street .

15 So they began by inviting Father Grumbler to sit down to the table , and brought out the best wine in the cellar , hoping it might loosen his tongue .
16 But Father Grumbler was wiser than they gave him credit for , and though they tried in all manner of ways to find out who had given him the basket , he put them off , and kept his secret to himself .
17 Unluckily , though he did not SPEAK , he did drink , and it was not long before he fell fast asleep .
18 Then the woman fetched from her kitchen a basket , so like the magic one that no one , without looking very closely , could tell the difference , and placed it in Father Grumbler 's hand , while she hid the other carefully away .
19 It was dinner time when the man awoke , and , jumping up hastily , he set out for home , where he found all the children gathered round a basin of thin soup , and pushing their wooden bowls forward , hoping to have the first spoonful .
20 Their father burst into the midst of them , bearing his basket , and crying : ` Do n't spoil your appetites , children , with that stuff .

12 Then the woman fetched from her kitchen a basket , so like the magic one that no one , without looking very closely , could tell the difference , and placed it in Father Grumbler 's hand , while she hid the other carefully away .
13 It was dinner time when the man awoke , and , jumping up hastily , he set out for home , where he found all the children gathered round a basin of thin soup , and pushing their wooden bowls forward , hoping to have the first spoonful .
14 Their father burst into the midst of them , bearing his basket , and crying : ` Do n't spoil your appetites , children , with that stuff .
15 Do you see this basket ?
16 Well , I have only got to say , `` Little basket , little basket , do your duty , '' and you will see what will happen .
17 Now you shall say it instead of me , for a treat . '
18 The children , wondering and delighted , repeated the words , but nothing happened .
19 Again and again they tried , but the basket was only a basket , with a few scales of fish sticking to the bottom , for the innkeeper 's wife had taken it to market the day before .
20 ` What is the matter with the thing ? '
21 cried the father at last , snatching the XXXXX from them , and turning it all over , grumbling and swearing while he did so , under the eyes of his astonished wife and children , who did not know whether to cry or to laugh .	basket		asking|basket|chairs|kitchen|matter|rolls|street|tables|wine|words

1 Eh ? '
2 And without waiting for an answer he whispered to the basket : ` Little basket , little basket , do your duty . '
3 The innkeeper and his wife thought that their customer had gone suddenly mad , and watched him closely , ready to spring on him if he became violent ; but both instinctively jumped backwards , nearly into the fire , as rolls and fishes of every kind came tumbling out of the basket , covering the tables and chairs and the floor , and even overflowing into the street .
4 ` Be quick , be quick , and pick them up , ' cried the man .
5 ` And if these are not enough , there are plenty more to be had for the asking . '
6 The innkeeper and his wife did not need telling twice .
7 Down they went on their knees and gathered up everything they could lay hands on .
8 But busy though they seemed , they found time to whisper to each other : ` If we can only get hold of that basket it will make our fortune ! '
9 So they began by inviting Father Grumbler to sit down to the table , and brought out the best wine in the cellar , hoping it might loosen his tongue .

7 ` Can I do anything for you , Father Grumbler ? '
8 asked the innkeeper 's wife in her softest voice . '

11 ` Why , what are you talking about ? '
12 answered she .

14 And though Father Grumbler DID look , it was quite true that none was to be seen .
